Analyze the following desire descriptions and extract any factual information that should be recorded as beliefs.

Desire Descriptions:
- Complete the task described in /instruction/task.md inside docker container 'hr-create-employee-manual'. Use available tools to inspect instructions, edit files in /workspace, run commands, and verify results. The rocketchat login is theagentcompany and the password is theagentcompany

Extract ONLY concrete, factual information explicitly stated in the desires, such as:
- File paths or directory paths (e.g., "repository path is /path/to/repo")
- Names or identifiers (e.g., "the project is called X")
- URLs or endpoints
- Specific values or configurations mentioned
- Any other concrete facts that would be useful context

Do NOT extract:
- The goals or objectives themselves (these are desires, not beliefs)
- Inferred or assumed information not explicitly stated
- Vague or subjective statements

IMPORTANT: Each belief MUST have exactly these three fields:
- "name": A concise identifier string (e.g., "repo_path", "project_name", "target_url")
- "value": The actual value as a string (e.g., "/path/to/repo", "my-project", "https://api.example.com")
- "certainty": A float between 0.0 and 1.0 (use 1.0 for explicitly stated facts)

Example of CORRECT format:
{
  "beliefs": [
    {"name": "repo_path", "value": "/Users/douglas/code/masters/pydantic-ai-bdi", "certainty": 1.0},
    {"name": "repo_name", "value": "pydantic-ai-bdi", "certainty": 1.0}
  ],
  "explanation": "Extracted repository path and name from desire description."
}

Example of INCORRECT format (DO NOT USE):
{
  "beliefs": [{"repo_path": "/path", "repo_name": "project"}]
}

If no factual information can be extracted, return an empty beliefs list with an explanation.

        Step type: Descriptive step

        Recent step history:
        Step 0: Use run_in_tac to read the instruction file contents with command `cat /instruction/task.md` so the exact requirements text is available for interpretation. - Success

        Evaluate if the step successfully achieved its original objective.

        Assessment Guidelines:

        FOR TOOL CALL STEPS:
        - If the tool executed and returned data (not an error message), mark as SUCCESS
        - The result may include analysis or discussion of the data - this is normal and doesn't indicate failure
        - Only mark as FAILED if the tool returned an error, exception, or "not found" type message

        FOR CHECK/VERIFY STEPS:
        - If the result provides a definitive answer (yes/no, found/not found, true/false), mark as SUCCESS

        FOR DESCRIPTIVE STEPS (no tool call):
        - If the step produced a concrete outcome or information, mark as SUCCESS
        - If the step only discussed what should be done without doing it, mark as FAILED

        FOR ALL STEPS:
        - Ignore verbose explanations or analysis in the result - focus on whether the objective was met
        - If the result explicitly states an error occurred, mark as FAILED
        - If uncertain, prefer SUCCESS over FAILURE (be lenient)

        Provide your assessment:
        - success: true if the step achieved its objective, false if it clearly failed
        - reason: brief explanation (especially important if failed)

        - Do NOT emit synonyms for existing belief names (reuse the same belief name when possible).

        IMPORTANT: Each belief MUST have exactly these three fields:

        Example of CORRECT format:
        {
          "beliefs": [

        {

        Evaluate if the step successfully achieved its original objective.

        Assessment Guidelines:

        FOR TOOL CALL STEPS:
        - If the tool executed and returned data (not an error message), mark as SUCCESS
        - The result may include analysis or discussion of the data - this is normal and doesn't indicate failure
        - Only mark as FAILED if the tool returned an error, exception, or "not found" type message

        FOR CHECK/VERIFY STEPS:
        - If the result provides a definitive answer (yes/no, found/not found, true/false), mark as SUCCESS

        FOR DESCRIPTIVE STEPS (no tool call):
        - If the step produced a concrete outcome or information, mark as SUCCESS
        - If the step only discussed what should be done without doing it, mark as FAILED

        FOR ALL STEPS:
        - Ignore verbose explanations or analysis in the result - focus on whether the objective was met
        - If the result explicitly states an error occurred, mark as FAILED
        - If uncertain, prefer SUCCESS over FAILURE (be lenient)

        Provide your assessment:
        - success: true if the step achieved its objective, false if it clearly failed
        - reason: brief explanation (especially important if failed)

# Employee Manual

## 1. Company Values
At The Agent Company, our values guide how we collaborate, serve customers, and grow as a team:
- **Integrity:** We act honestly, take accountability, and do the right thing even when no one is watching.
- **Customer Focus:** We prioritize customer outcomes and continuously improve our service quality.
- **Collaboration:** We work across teams with transparency, mutual respect, and shared ownership.
- **Innovation:** We encourage thoughtful experimentation, practical creativity, and continuous learning.
- **Inclusion:** We foster an environment where every employee is treated with dignity and has equal opportunity to contribute.

## 2. Code of Conduct
All employees are expected to uphold professional standards at all times.

### 2.1 Professional Behavior
- Treat colleagues, customers, vendors, and partners respectfully.
- Maintain clear, professional communication in person and online.
- Avoid harassment, discrimination, bullying, or retaliation of any kind.

### 2.2 Ethics and Compliance
- Follow applicable laws, regulations, and internal requirements.
- Disclose conflicts of interest to your manager or HR.
- Never offer, request, or accept inappropriate gifts or favors.

### 2.3 Data and Confidentiality
- Protect confidential company and customer information.
- Access only the data needed to perform your role.
- Report suspected data breaches or security incidents immediately.

### 2.4 Workplace Safety and Reporting
- Follow workplace safety instructions and emergency procedures.
- Report unsafe conditions, policy violations, or misconduct promptly.
- Use designated reporting channels, including HR and management.

## 3. Operational Procedures
This section outlines core day-to-day practices for smooth operations.

### 3.1 Work Hours and Attendance
- Standard working hours are defined by department and role.
- Employees are expected to be punctual and notify managers of delays or absences.
- Time off requests should be submitted in advance whenever possible.

### 3.2 Communication and Collaboration
- Use approved communication tools for business operations.
- Keep project updates current and escalate blockers early.
- Document key decisions to support team continuity.

### 3.3 Performance and Development
- Employees participate in regular check-ins and performance reviews.
- Goals should be clear, measurable, and aligned with team priorities.
- Training and development are encouraged and supported by managers.

### 3.4 IT and System Use
- Use company devices and systems responsibly.
- Keep passwords secure and enable required security controls.
- Software installations must follow IT approval processes.

## 4. Employee Benefits
The company offers benefits to support employee well-being and long-term success. Benefit eligibility may vary by location and employment status.

### 4.1 Health and Wellness
- Medical, dental, and vision coverage (where applicable).
- Employee wellness resources and mental health support.

### 4.2 Time-Off Benefits
- Paid time off (PTO), company holidays, and sick leave.
- Additional leave options may include parental, bereavement, or personal leave.

### 4.3 Financial and Retirement Support
- Retirement savings options and employer contributions where offered.
- Payroll, expense reimbursement, and financial planning resources.

### 4.4 Learning and Growth
- Role-relevant learning opportunities, mentoring, and skill-building support.
- Internal mobility support and career development planning.

## 5. Company Policies
These policies establish consistent expectations across the organization.

### 5.1 Equal Employment Opportunity
The company is committed to fair hiring, development, and advancement practices and prohibits discrimination based on protected characteristics.

### 5.2 Anti-Harassment and Anti-Discrimination
Harassment and discrimination are prohibited. All complaints are reviewed promptly and handled confidentially to the extent possible.

### 5.3 Remote and Hybrid Work
Remote/hybrid arrangements may be available based on role and business needs. Employees must maintain productivity, availability, and data security standards.

### 5.4 Leave and Accommodation
Employees may request statutory or company-supported leave and workplace accommodations through HR in accordance with applicable laws.

### 5.5 Disciplinary Process
Policy violations may result in corrective action, up to and including termination, based on severity and frequency.

## 6. Suggested Additions (If Not Covered in TAC_overview.md)
If source content is limited, consider adding these sections to strengthen the manual:
- **Compensation Philosophy and Pay Practices** (pay cycles, overtime, bonus eligibility)
- **Travel and Expense Policy** (approvals, reimbursable costs, submission timelines)
- **Procurement and Approval Matrix** (spending authority by role)
- **Information Security Policy Detail** (data classification, retention, access reviews)
- **Incident Response and Business Continuity** (escalation path and recovery expectations)
- **Whistleblower and Non-Retaliation Policy** (confidential reporting pathways)
- **Offboarding and Asset Return Procedure**
- **Acknowledgment Form** for employee signature and policy receipt

## 7. Document Governance
- **Owner:** Human Resources Team
- **Review Cycle:** Annual or as required by legal/operational changes
- **Effective Date:** [Insert Date]
- **Version:** 1.0

          "explanation": "Extracted repository path and confirmed commits exist."
        }

        Example of INCORRECT format (DO NOT USE):
        {
          "beliefs": [{"repo_path": "/path", "has_commits": true}]
        }
